Re: Project review under Section 106 of the National Historic Preservation Act of 1966 and the
Antiquities Code of Texas
Draft Report Review Marine Archeological Survey of Proposed North Jetty Sand Source,
Galveston, Texas
Texas Antiquities Permit No. 7560, Tracking No. 201701427
ClAP, GLO
Dear Mr. Gearhart:
This letter serves as comment on the proposed federal undertaking from the State Historic
Preservation Officer, the Executive Director of the Texas Historical Commission (THC). As the
state agency responsible for administering the Antiquities Code of Texas, these comments also
provide recommendations on compliance with state antiquities laws and regulations.
The review staff, led by State Marine Archeologist Amy A. Borgens has reviewed the draft
report. Surveying and Mapping LLC conducted a marine archeological remote-sensing survey of
the north side of the Galveston entrance jetties in February 2016 for habitat restoration projects
at Bolivar Peninsula. According to the report findings the survey discovered 26 geophysical
targets initially recommended as significant anomalies for avoidance.
At the request of the client, 14 of these 26 targets were to be avoided without additional
investigation and 12 targets were selected for ground-truthing through diver reconnaissance and
probing. The investigation of these 12 targets determined that 9 were not cultural resources and 3
(Mag 10,13, and 24) are wooden hulled s~pwrecks that have the potential to be State Antiquities
Landmarks and/or are eligible for the Natirnal Register of Historic Places. In total, 17 of the 26
geophysical targets are recommended for avoidance. The THC [concurs with the author's
recommendations. Anomalies Mag l/Son
1, Mag 2/Sonar 2, Mag 3, Mag 4, Mag 5/ Sonar 15,
Mag 7, Mag 8/Sonar 3, Mag 9/Sonar4,
ag, 10, Mag 11, Mag 13, Mag 15/Sonar 6, Mag
16/Sonar 7, Mag 17/Sonar 8, Mag 20, M g 23/ Sonar 9, and Mag 24 must be avoided by the
required 50 m avoidance margin. If the
omalies cannot be avoided, additional archeological
investigation will be required.

As has become standard for such sand so rce projects, a follow-up survey is needed to assess
I

any impact to the sources of recommended anomalies within two months after the completion of
dredging. The standard avoidance zone was developed for projects with more controllable
D-5 | Page

Page 2 of3
THC Review Comments Permit 7560

impacts, such as drilling wells or laying pipelines. Because this undertaking involves dredging
away much of the accumulated sediment over a large area, the avoided anomaly locations may
become exposed high points on the bottom within the perimeter of the dredged area. These high
points may be subject to considerable erosion, thus removing the protective layer of sediments
and exposing the sources of anomalies.
Additional comments for the report are included in Appendix A and can be included in the final
draft submitted to the THe. We look forward to receiving the final report.
Thank you for your cooperation in this federal and state review process, and for your efforts to
preserve the irreplaceable heritage of Texas. If you have any questions concerning our review
or if we can be of further assistance, please contact Amy Borgens at 512-463-9505.

Sincerely,

Mark Wolfe
State Historic Preservation Officer

Appendix A
1) ClAP is a federally funded program and the funding is allocated to Texas and
other states from federal sources. The language regarding Section 106 on page
2 needs to be expanded to include funding and not just permitting. This
project is already attached to Section 106 of the National Historic Preservation
Act though the federal funding.
2) On page 25, please include the citation for the ferro-concrete wreck. This is:
Arnold III, J. Barto
1999
Reconnaissance Surveys of Shipwrecks: Interim Report for 1998
as Required by MOU and Permit 1901. Institute of Nautical Archeology,
College Stattion, TX. Document on file at the Texas Historical Commission.
3) You may want to add that additional survey data was collected on City of
Waco in 2012 which demonstrated the site is more exposed than in the past.
This work was conducted under THC's annual permit 2035 through a
partnership with NOAA. There is a citation for this if needed that can be
provided:
Borgens, Amy A.
2013
Descent into Darkness: THC Assists with Two Historic Shipwreck
Investigations in Low-Visibility Waters. Medallion (Spring):10-11.
4) In the abstract, introduction, and conclusion, please clearly list the
names/labels of the significant targets that have been recommended for
avoidance.
